If we still have desired endpoints to add and slices marked for update,\n   550→\t//    iterate through the slices and fill them up with the desired endpoints.\n   551→\tif desiredSet.Len() > 0 && sliceNamesToUpdate.Len() > 0 {\n   552→\t\tslices := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   553→\t\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesToUpdate.UnsortedList() {\n   554→\t\t\tslices = append(slices, slicesByName[sliceName])\n   555→\t\t}\n   556→\t\t// Sort endpoint slices by length so we're filling up the fullest ones\n   557→\t\t// first.\n   558→\t\tsort.Sort(endpointSliceEndpointLen(slices))\n   559→\n   560→\t\t// Iterate through slices and fill them up with desired endpoints.\n   561→\t\tfor _, slice := range slices {\n   562→\t\t\tfor desiredSet.Len() > 0 && len(slice.Endpoints) < int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice) {\n   563→\t\t\t\tendpoint, _ := desiredSet.PopAny()\n   564→\t\t\t\tslice.Endpoints = append(slice.Endpoints, *endpoint)\n   565→\t\t\t}\n   566→\t\t}\n   567→\t}\n   568→\n   569→\t// 3. If there are still desired endpoints left at this point, we try to fit\n   570→\t//    the endpoints in a single existing slice. If there are no slices with\n   571→\t//    that capacity, we create new slices for the endpoints.\n   572→\tslicesToCreate := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   573→\n   574→\tfor desiredSet.Len() > 0 {\n   575→\t\tvar sliceToFill *discovery.EndpointSlice\n   576→\n   577→\t\t// If the remaining amounts of endpoints is smaller than the max\n   578→\t\t// endpoints per slice and we have slices that haven't already been\n   579→\t\t// filled, try to fit them in one.\n   580→\t\tif desiredSet.Len() < int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice) && sliceNamesUnchanged.Len() > 0 {\n   581→\t\t\tunchangedSlices := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   582→\t\t\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesUnchanged.UnsortedList() {\n   583→\t\t\t\tunchangedSlices = append(unchangedSlices, slicesByName[sliceName])\n   584→\t\t\t}\n   585→\t\t\tsliceToFill = getSliceToFill(unchangedSlices, desiredSet.Len(), int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice))\n   586→\t\t}\n   587→\n   588→\t\t// If we didn't find a sliceToFill, generate a new empty one.\n   589→\t\tif sliceToFill == nil {\n   590→\t\t\tsliceToFill = newEndpointSlice(logger, service, endpointMeta, r.controllerName)\n   591→\t\t} else {\n   592→\t\t\t// deep copy required to modify this slice.\n   593→\t\t\tsliceToFill = sliceToFill.DeepCopy()\n   594→\t\t\tslicesByName[sliceToFill.Name] = sliceToFill\n   595→\t\t}\n   596→\n   597→\t\t// Fill the slice up with remaining endpoints.\n   598→\t\tfor desiredSet.Len() > 0 && len(sliceToFill.Endpoints) < int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice) {\n   599→\t\t\tendpoint, _ := desiredSet.PopAny()\n   600→\t\t\tsliceToFill.Endpoints = append(sliceToFill.Endpoints, *endpoint)\n   601→\t\t}\n   602→\n   603→\t\t// New slices will not have a Name set, use this to determine whether\n   604→\t\t// this should be an update or create.\n   605→\t\tif sliceToFill.Name != \"\" {\n   606→\t\t\tsliceNamesToUpdate.Insert(sliceToFill.Name)\n   607→\t\t\tsliceNamesUnchanged.Delete(sliceToFill.Name)\n   608→\t\t} else {\n   609→\t\t\tslicesToCreate = append(slicesToCreate, sliceToFill)\n   610→\t\t}\n   611→\t}\n   612→\n   613→\t// Build slicesToUpdate from slice names.\n   614→\tslicesToUpdate := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   615→\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesToUpdate.UnsortedList() {\n   616→\t\tslicesToUpdate = append(slicesToUpdate, slicesByName[sliceName])\n   617→\t}\n   618→\n   619→\t// Build slicesToDelete from slice names.\n   620→\tslicesToDelete := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n   621→\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesToDelete.UnsortedList() {\n   622→\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete, slicesByName[sliceName])\n   623→\t}\n   624→\n   625→\treturn slicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate, slicesToDelete, numAdded, numRemoved\n   626→}\n   627→\n Kubernetes controller framework pattern that differs from controller-runtime. Here's how it works:\\n\\n## Controller Registration Pattern\\n\\n### 1. Reconciler Interface Definition\\nThe Reconciler concept is implemented as controller structs like `DeploymentController` (kubernetes/kubernetes:pkg/controller/deployment/deployment_controller.go:66-98). The struct contains:\\n- Kubernetes clients and listers from k8s.io/client-go\\n- A work queue (workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface) for items to reconcile\\n- Event recorder for publishing events\\n- A syncHandler function that implements the reconciliation logic\\n\\n### 2. SetupWithManager Equivalent\\nInstead of SetupWithManager(), Kubernetes uses a two-step initialization pattern:\\n\\n**Step 1: Controller Instantiation** (kubernetes/kubernetes:pkg/controller/deployment/deployment_controller.go:100-159)\\n- NewDeploymentController() factory function creates the controller instance\\n- Registers informer event handlers (AddEventHandler) for Deployments, ReplicaSets, and Pods\\n- Each handler (AddFunc, UpdateFunc, DeleteFunc) enqueues items for reconciliation\\n- Stores informer listers and synced signals for dependency tracking\\n\\n**Step 2: Manager Integration** (kubernetes/kubernetes:cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/apps.go:106-119)\\n- startDeploymentController() function instantiates the controller\\n- Calls dc.Run(ctx, workers) to start the reconciliation loop\\n- The manager passes a ControllerContext containing InformerFactory, ClientBuilder, and ComponentConfig\\n\\n### 3. Manager's Reconcile Loop Wiring\\nThe wiring happens in the controller manager:\\n\\n**ControllerContext** (kubernetes/kubernetes:cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:366-401) serves as the manager equivalent, providing:\\n- ClientBuilder for Kubernetes API clients\\n- InformerFactory for creating Informers and Listers\\n- ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory for generic resource handling\\n- InformersStarted signal for synchronization\\n\\n**Control Flow Chain**:\\n1. Run() function (kubernetes/kubernetes:cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:175) creates ControllerContext via CreateControllerContext()\\n2. StartControllers() (kubernetes/kubernetes:cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go) iterates through controller descriptors and calls their initFunc\\n3. Each controller's initFunc (e.g., startDeploymentController) instantiates the controller and calls Run()\\n4. InformerFactory.Start() begins syncing informers\\n5. Controllers process work queue items in a worker loop (kubernetes/kubernetes:pkg/controller/deployment/deployment_controller.go:162-185)\\n\\n### 4.
